{\"address\":{\"all\":{\"data\":[],\"status\":null},\"data\":{},\"new\":null},\"articles\":{\"all\":{\"data\":[\"how-to-lose-stubborn-fat\",\"top-3-exercises-for-bigger-and-rounder-butt\",\"ultimate-health-fitness-guide\",\"smart-goals\",\"the-science-of-motivation\",\"fresh-vs-frozen-fruits-vegetables\",\"how-to-go-vegan-vegetarian\",\"if-it-fits-your-macros\",\"carb-cycling-keto-diets\",\"how-to-stay-healthy-at-the-grocery-store\"],\"status\":null},\"data\":{\"how-to-lose-stubborn-fat\":{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Article\",\"data\":{\"id\":75,\"className\":\"Article\",\"title\":\"How To Lose Stubborn Fat: Visceral And Subcutaneous Fat\",\"description\":\"Weight loss is a goal for many people and it can turn into a fight against your own body. Gymaholic shows you how to break down that persistent body fat!\",\"img\":\"https://cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/26-how-to-lose-stubborn-fat/1-how-to-lose-stubborn-fat.jpg\",\"shareImg\":\"https://cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/26-how-to-lose-stubborn-fat/share-how-to-lose-stubborn-fat-2.jpg\",\"slug\":\"how-to-lose-stubborn-fat\",\"publishedAt\":\"2017-03-29T00:08:53.715Z\",\"content\":\"# Fat Loss and Stubborn Fat\\n## Why so persistent, and how do I get rid of it? \\n\\n\\nWeight loss is a goal for many people, and the process of losing weight, or specifically **losing fat** can turn into a fight against your own body. Whether your reason for targeting that **stubborn fat** is **health, happiness, aesthetics or competition**; it may not be easy, but it’s certainly possible to lose that weight!\\n\\nGymaholic shows you how to **break down and keep off that persistent body fat!**\\n\\n\\n![Woman with a belly fat](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/26-how-to-lose-stubborn-fat/belly-fat.jpg \\\"Belly fat\\\")\\n\\n\\n### What is Stubborn Fat?\\nFirst, before anything else we must address those goal differences between the people reading this article, because there are two main groups of people looking for **fat loss**:\\n\\n- Those who are overweight or obese, who are attempting to get their health and/or weight under control.\\n\\n- Those who are generally healthy, lean and/or muscular but want to take things further for their own pleasure/aesthetics or competitive reasons. \\n\\nThere are many who sit on the bridge between these two groups, who aren’t exactly overweight but may not necessarily be “healthy” either. They may just have a little excess fat they feel like getting rid of. \\n\\n\\n#### Why does it matter? \\nIt’s important to understand which group you’re closest to because the cause of stubborn fat and the methods to deal with it can be different between these groups. Thus, your current situation and what you perceive as **stubborn fat** is needed to direct you to the solution. \\n\\n\\n### Why So Stubborn? \\nOf course, the main reasons fat is stored in the body is for **excess energy** and **metabolism control**. Fat is stored in **adipocytes**, or fat cells, which group together to form **adipose tissue**. It releases hormones like leptin which controls our appetite. \\n\\nThere are two main types of fat tissue: **visceral fat** and **subcutaneous fat**. \\n\\n\\n#### Visceral Fat \\n**Visceral fat** is also known as **organ or abdominal fat**. It is a dense fat that, as the name suggests, is tucked in and around our organs and can build up in the abdominal area. Excess visceral fat is linked to type 2 diabetes, insulin resistance and inflammation! \\n\\n\\n#### Subcutaneous Fat\\n**Subcutaneous fat** is the fat under our skin. It’s softer, that ‘fat’ that we can see and pinch on our bodies. This fat is not necessarily bad fat, and that’s one of the reasons why it can be the harder of the two to get rid of. It has a very prominent role in our body’s **survival mechanisms and is heavily linked to reproduction**. \\n\\n\\n#### It’s Instinctive! \\nSince we are hardwired to survive, our body likes to keep an excess of stored energy in the form of fat, and since our primary goal as a species is technically to reproduce, our reproductive area is where it tends to settle. \\n\\nIn women the problem areas tend to be the hips, thighs and butt, and in men it is around the lower abdomen. When women get older and hit menopause the weight also shifts to the abdomen. \\n\\n**Excess weight, lack of physical activity and an unhealthy diet** can cause hormone imbalances and mess with reproduction. However, **very high levels of activity and very restricted diets** can have a similar or more prominent effect, especially in women! \\n\\nIf the body fat percentage gets low enough, the body’s survival instincts kick in and priority becomes your ‘survival’, and energy is moved away from reproduction. This is why some women who are heavily active can lose their periods, or experience them far less often! \\n\\n\\n![Couple with flat belly](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/26-how-to-lose-stubborn-fat/couple-flat-belly.jpg \\\"Fitness couple with flat belly\\\")\\n\\n\\n### The solution\\nAs mentioned, the solution varies depending on your situation and goals because everyone is different. Although there are a few factors like sex and genetics that are out of your control, there are many other factors like your **diet and exercise habits** that you can control! \\n\\nYou can even **control the release of certain hormones** in your body indirectly through some methods. Since adipose tissue releases hormones like **leptin** to control our appetite, and the digestion and absorption of food prompts the release of **insulin**, understanding those hormones can be beneficial to your success! \\n\\nTo learn more about leptin: <a href=\\\"/articles/cheat-meals-and-fat-loss\\\" title=\\\"Cheat meals and fat loss\\\">Cheat Meals and Fat Loss</a>\\nTo learn more about insulin:  <a href=\\\"/articles/fat-loss-plateau-understanding-insulin-sensitivity\\\" title=\\\"Fat loss plateau: understand insulin sensitivty\\\">Fat Loss Plateau: Understanding Insulin Sensitivity</a>\\n\\n\\n### Weight & Health Focus\\nThose who are overweight or considered ‘unhealthy’ will often have an excess of **both visceral fat and subcutaneous fat**. Visceral fat is the first issue, and the cause of most of those health risks! In order to target excess visceral fat you need to achieve **moderate weight loss**. \\n\\nAttempting to lose a lot of weight in a short period of time by heavily increasing exercise and heavily cutting the diet may benefit in the short term, but visceral fat can rebound hard and it’s very likely the weight lost and health risks will return!\\n\\n**Slowly adding in moderate exercise to your routine and subbing healthier options gradually will target visceral fat**. This is extremely important because when visceral fat loss occurs:\\n\\n- Inflammation & Stress Decreases \\n- Metabolism Response/Control Improves \\n- Hormone Response/Control Improves\\n- Subcutaneous fat becomes easier to lose! \\n\\nUnfortunately, **visceral fat loss is gradual and not always visible**! Because of this, people think that their methods are not working, or they get impatient and attempt to find a fast fix for more unhealthy, rapid weight loss that in the end, won’t fix anything at all. \\n\\nIf you need help making reasonable, achievable goals, check out <a href=\\\"/articles/smart-goals\\\" title=\\\"Smart goals\\\">SMART Goals!</a>\\n\\n\\n### Gaining Muscle\\nSome who are at a moderate weight, and begin incorporating exercise into their routine also may not see results right away. As you begin exercising you may be **losing fat and gaining muscle simultaneously**. \\n\\nDue to muscle (also referred to as fat free mass) being heavier than fat, your weight may not be changing, but the ratio of fat mass to fat free mass and the composition of your body might be! \\n\\nAs your muscle mass increases, you require more energy to maintain it, so you will also burn more fat! **HIIT** (High Intensity Interval Training) can target **both visceral and subcutaneous fat**, and it’s a great way to build muscle and stamina while burning fat quickly and efficiently! \\n\\n\\n### Plateaus\\nThose who are somewhere in the middle often get ‘stuck’ at a certain weight. At one point they were losing consistent weight on their healthy new routine, and then suddenly their results fizzle out and stop. \\n\\nMore than likely you have hit a fat loss plateau! This just means that your body has become used to your routine, so you need to change it up in order to wake up your metabolism again! \\n \\nTo learn more about how to break through a plateau you can check out <a href=\\\"/articles/fat-loss-plateau-understanding-insulin-sensitivity\\\" title=\\\"Fat loss plateau: understand insulin sensitivty\\\">Fat Loss Plateau: Understanding Insulin Sensitivity</a> and <a href=\\\"/articles/ultimate-progress-guide\\\" title=\\\"Ultimate progress guide\\\">The Ultimate Progress Guide!</a>\\n\\n\\n### Lean & Muscular Focus\\nThose who are already fairly healthy and lean are usually aiming to **clear some stubborn fat to show more muscle definition**, or get to a weight that they prefer personally, even though they may be healthy in their current state. \\n\\nIt is very unlikely that someone who is already fairly healthy and lean would have any issue with visceral fat, and their main target will be subcutaneous fat centered around the problem areas listed above for men and women. \\n\\nYou **cannot spot reduce fat**, so attempting to work the muscles in a problem area more will not often make it go away. The main solution is just to continue lowering your body fat percentage gradually.\\n\\nUnfortunately, the leaner you get and the lower your body fat percentage, **the faster your body will adjust to change (hit fat loss plateaus)** and the **harder it will fight against you** to keep that remaining fat. \\n\\nAlthough it is not recommended to try any dramatic increases in exercise or decrease in calorie consumption (the rebound can be just as dramatic!), it is recommended to change your routine as frequently as possible! \\n\\n- Trying a new sport instead of going to the gym \\n- Running outside on uneven ground instead of a treadmill \\n- Try **HIIT** (High Intensity Interval Training) for a metabolism boost\\n- Trying new recipes and new foods\\n- Shock your system with <a href=\\\"/articles/cheat-meals-and-fat-loss\\\" title=\\\"Cheat meals and fat loss\\\">Cheat Meals</a>\\n\\nThis has to do with overcoming those **fat loss plateaus** and controlling hormone release to increase the use of fat as fuel. You could also try **<a href=\\\"/articles/intermittent-fasting\\\" title=\\\"Intermittent fasting\\\">intermittent fasting</a>** as another method of controlling the release of hormones and what your body uses as fuel. \\n\\n\\n### In Conclusion\\nThe body is extremely complex, but we know a lot more now about how it works. It’s up to you to apply that knowledge to get the results you want! It’s important to:\\n\\n- Figure out why your body is storing that fat\\n- Know your target (or both?) \\n- Create a plan for the solution\\n- Gradual healthy diet and exercise changes\\n- Gain Muscle & HITT\\n- Don’t get discouraged! Trust your body is changing.\\n- Understand and control fat loss hormones\\n- Change your routine!\\n\\nKnowing your opponent and the weapons you have in your arsenal can ensure victory. Keep fighting towards your goals and you’ll achieve them!   \\n\\n\\n### Questions & Comments\\nIf you have any question or simply want to talk about your experience, don't hesitate to comment below. T15:15:27.688Z\",\"twitterId\":\"2291371556\",\"twitterToken\":\"2291371556-njiTzYxajWlY1VwMfAJWFW0QL1Lrl9IFnDbjjWq\",\"twitterEmail\":\"contact@gymaholic.co\",\"lastName\":\"\",\"firstName\":\"Gymaholic\",\"name\":\"gymaholic\",\"role\":1,\"verifiedAt\":\"2017-04-21T15:15:27.688Z\",\"avatar\":\"https://pbs.twimg.com/profile_images/511101318329413632/OO3b76iA_normal.jpeg\",\"bio\":\"Inspire How to Set S.M.A.R.T Goals and Stay Motivated\",\"description\":\"Get S.M.A.R.T, Get Happy: how to make goals you can achieve, so you can dream bigger, reach higher and work harder towards your success and happiness. \",\"img\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/24-smart-goals/1-smart-goals.jpg\",\"shareImg\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/24-smart-goals/share-smart-goals-1.jpg\",\"slug\":\"smart-goals\",\"featuredAt\":\"2016-12-21T05:17:41.000Z\",\"publishedAt\":\"2016-12-21T05:17:37.562Z\",\"content\":\"# Get S.M.A.R.T, Get Happy\\n## How to Set S.M.A.R.T Goals and Stay Motivated\\n\\n\\nWe all have goals and aspirations that drive us, but some people seem to have this overpowering determination to succeed with positive energy to spare. Those people motivate themselves in the right way by having ** strong motivating factors ** and setting **reasonable goals**. \\n\\nWe already talked about some strong motivators in the **<a href=\\\"/articles/the-science-of-motivation\\\" title=\\\"The science of motivation\\\">Science of Motivation</a>**, but finding and keeping your motivation is more than just knowing what you’re fighting for. \\n\\nThe secret to **staying motivated** is making the right goals that enforce a **positive mindset** and energize you to keep going. Gymaholic shows you how to make goals you can achieve, so you can **dream bigger, reach higher and work harder** towards your own success and happiness. \\n\\n\\n![Accomplishment](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/24-smart-goals/man-setting-smart-goals.jpg \\\"Man setting smart goals\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Get S.M.A.R.T\\nPeople always say “I’m going to… --Be healthier!” “--Work out more!” “--Eat better!”. To me, these are not goals. These are large, vague statements that don’t have the same meaning for all of us, so we can’t use them as a goal point. \\n\\nPut it this way. If there was a GPS system to guide you to your goal, you’d have to input an address or landmark to find a route to get you there. Instead of inputting a location, you’re just shouting “Take me there!” with no real definition of what or where ‘there’ is. \\n\\nYou need to create goals you can **visualize and achieve**. The best goals are **Specific, Measurable, Attainable, Realistic, and Timely (S.M.A.R.T)**\\n\\n#### Specific\\n\\nThe more specific the goal is, the better. Where are you going to work out? What exercises are you going to do? What do you plan to eat today? The more detail you have and the more questions you ask yourself, the easier it is to visualize and plan how you’re going to execute it. \\n\\n#### Measurable\\nEverything is **measurable**. How many reps, how many sets? How long are you playing/practicing for? How many times per week? How much are you eating? How often are you going to eat it? How many weeks/months will you do it for? Even vague measurements are a start, and better than none at all. \\n\\n#### Attainable & Realistic\\nLogically, you need to think about whether you can **attain** or **achieve** this goal. This is not about discouraging yourself by saying ‘I can’t’, unless you **physically cannot**. Your goals need to be something **realistic** that you can see yourself accomplishing, because if you can’t, it’s possible that the goal is too large, and is more suited as a further goal, with more steps in between.\\n\\nCan you afford a gym membership? Maybe do bodyweight workouts at home instead, for now. Is losing 20 lbs in a week unreasonable? Yes. Since technically speaking, most people can only healthily lose around 2-3lbs maximum in one week. Will you really start eating 4 servings of fruit a day, when right now you usually have 1? Maybe work up to 2 servings, a few times a week first. \\n\\n#### Timely\\nMaking your goals **timely** or ‘**time-bound**’ is focused on having a start and end point to your goal. **Goals should not go on indefinitely**. It’s like making a checklist and never being able to check anything off. It is boring and unmotivating. \\n\\nOf course it’s great if you have a habit of going to the gym twice a week, and you don’t plan on stopping. If it’s already a solidified habit, don’t consider it a goal. Now that you’ve found some rhythm, focus on taking the next step up in your exercise routine, or increasing how often you go to the gym, maybe add in some healthy eating goals. Find something new to work towards. \\n\\n\\n![Happy](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/24-smart-goals/happily-after.jpg \\\"Happily ever after\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Get Happy!\\nHow do SMART goals make you happy? Small shocks of **positive reinforcement** can do wonders for your motivation and confidence. It’s a small voice telling you that you’ve completed these goals, which means you can complete more goals and set your sights higher. It prompts you to believe in yourself and work harder.\\n\\n**There is nothing wrong with reaching for extreme end goals and big changes to your body**, but you likely won’t see results right away, and it can take you a long time to reach that endpoint. \\n\\n**Slow progress is better than no progress**, and often it’s better to take baby steps towards that larger goal instead of only focusing on that end point and becoming overwhelmed and quitting, without accomplishing anything at all.\\n\\nIf you’ve decided your destination but it’s on the other side of the country, you wouldn’t just start driving and hope for the best. You plan your route to get there, with multiple stops along the way. As many have said, “**getting there is half the fun!**”, so don’t forget to stop and rest, appreciating all the steps you’ve taken and how they all add up. You’ll gain a lot of your experiences and knowledge along the way. \\n\\n\\n### Conclusion\\nThings won’t always go the way you want them to, and you’ll have to constantly re-evaluate and make new goals for yourself. Creating smaller Specific, Measurable, Attainable, Realistic and Timely goals gives you positive reinforcement, motivating and energizing you to keep working towards those larger end goals.  \\n\\n\\n**Get S.M.A.R.T, Get Happy!**\\n\\n\\n<iframe width=\\\"560\\\" height=\\\"315\\\" src=\\\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/bjymHT67YoQ\\\" frameborder=\\\"0\\\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-10-17T15:05:25.680Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-12-23T05:50:33.648Z\",\"userId\":56,\"categories\":[{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Category\",\"data\":{\"id\":2,\"className\":\"Category\",\"title\":\"Articles: Fitness\",\"description\":\"Fitness model interviews, workout advice and everything related to the fitness lifestyle. You have fitness goals? Gymaholic helps you achieve them.\",\"name\":\"fitness\",\"publishedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:22:47.280Z\",\"contentTitle\":\"Fitness Over Everything\",\"createdAt\":\"2015-09-21T02:11:40.791Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:22:47.417Z\",\"sectionId\":2,\"ArticleCategory\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-12-21T05:15:12.971Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-12-21T05:15:12.971Z\",\"articleId\":72,\"categoryId\":2},\"section\":{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Section\",\"data\":{\"id\":2,\"className\":\"Section\",\"name\":\"articles\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:22:46.996Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:22:46.996Z\"},\"cid\":6277}},\"cid\":6277}],\"tags\":[{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Tag\",\"data\":{\"id\":1851,\"className\":\"Tag\",\"name\":\"smart\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-02-08T17:40:01.396Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-02-08T17:40:01.396Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"articleId\":72,\"tagId\":1851}},\"cid\":29729},{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Tag\",\"data\":{\"id\":689,\"className\":\"Tag\",\"name\":\"happy\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:25:05.157Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:25:05.157Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"articleId\":72,\"tagId\":689}},\"cid\":29730},{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Tag\",\"data\":{\"id\":140,\"className\":\"Tag\",\"name\":\"goals\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:24:40.237Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:24:40.237Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"articleId\":72,\"tagId\":140}},\"cid\":29731},{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Tag\",\"data\":{\"id\":47,\"className\":\"Tag\",\"name\":\"article\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:24:36.614Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:24:36.614Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-12-21T04:31:36.114Z\",\"articleId\":72,\"tagId\":47}},\"cid\":29732}],\"user\":{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"User\",\"data\":{\"id\":56,\"className\":\"User\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-06-29T03:32:29.913Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2017-04-20T12:16:00.903Z\",\"email\":\"sara.pindera@gmail.com\",\"lastName\":\"Pindera\",\"firstName\":\"Sara\",\"name\":\"msmaddhatt\",\"role\":2,\"verifiedAt\":\"2017-04-20T12:16:00.903Z\",\"avatar\":\"https://static.tumblr.com/nc9sq5s/zQnojkn54/avatar_a42c77d7f844_128.png\",\"bio\":\"Bachelor of Science in Nutrition and Nutraceuticals. A Canadian with a love of food, fitness and health. \",\"website\":\"https://www.youtube.com/c/msmaddhatt/\",\"gender\":2,\"birthday\":\"1994-07-25T00:00:00.000Z\",\"height\":5.5,\"heightUnit\":1,\"weight\":120,\"weightUnit\":1,\"goal\":3,\"location\":\"CA\",\"timezone\":\"America/Toronto\"},\"cid\":2025}},\"cid\":1381},\"the-science-of-motivation\":{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Article\",\"data\":{\"id\":71,\"className\":\"Article\",\"title\":\"The Science of Motivation: Tips That Can Help You Succeed\",\"description\":\" The more you understand why you’re motivated to doing something, the more you challenge and enjoy yourself, and the more you’re likely to stick with it.\",\"img\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/23-the-science-of-motivation/1-the-science-of-motivation.jpg\",\"shareImg\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/23-the-science-of-motivation/share-the-science-of-motivation-1.jpg\",\"slug\":\"the-science-of-motivation\",\"publishedAt\":\"2016-10-19T03:15:23.702Z\",\"content\":\"# The Science of Motivation\\n## Strong Motivators That Can Help You Succeed\\n\\n\\nThere are many reasons why people do things like participate in sports, begin an exercise routine or try to make healthier food choices. Finding solid reasoning behind why you want to create a healthy lifestyle for yourself is almost as important as physically applying those changes to your diet and exercise. \\n\\nIt’s important because **the more you understand why you’re motivated** to doing something, **the more you challenge and enjoy yourself**, and the more you’re likely to stick with it. Gymaholic explains **the strongest motivators**, and how to use them to strengthen your drive to achieve your goals.\\n\\nYou may already know the primary reason(s) you exercise, but there are some motivating factors that are scientifically proven to work as better motivators than others. Our main motivations are generally separated into two categories, **intrinsic** and **extrinsic**.  \\n\\n\\n![Motivation Bubble](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/23-the-science-of-motivation/motivation-bubble.jpg \\\"Motivation and synonyms\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Intrinsic Motivation\\n**Intrinsic motivators** are the **strongest forces that drive people** to do things. You are intrinsically motivated when you voluntarily do something simply because you enjoy doing it, meaning you don’t need a threat of punishment or reward. There are three main intrinsic drives: The drive to **know**, to gain **accomplishments**, and be **stimulated**. \\n\\n#### Knowledge\\nKnowing what you are capable of, **learning** new things about your body and yourself, **exploring** and **understanding** how and why things work simply out of **curiosity** can help fulfill personal learning goals. Being taught how to properly perform an exercise by a trainer, participating in a new sport or trying a new move, and learning new recipes to see if they taste good and making use of new ingredients you’ve never tried before. \\n\\n#### Accomplishments\\nAccomplishments our need to be **unique**, **creative**, to **surpass ourselves** and **master a task**. Improving or mastering a difficult task can bring on a strong sense of personal satisfaction, like setting new personal records, memorizing a healthy, great tasting recipe that can blow your friends minds. **Challenging yourself** keep things interesting and motivates you to constantly create and reach new goals.\\n\\n#### Stimulation\\nStimulation is an extremely powerful motivator. Feeling great after you finally finish a long, hard workout, the adrenaline you get from playing a competitive sport, the feeling of playing with a team or overcoming a problem. Having fun and **enjoying what you’re doing** is key when it comes to these motivating factors. \\n\\n\\n### Extrinsic Motivation\\n**Extrinsic motivators** tend to be more shallow goals, which are **weaker, and can be broken more easily**. They are often used as a means to solve a problem, and not for your own sake of enjoyment. These also have three main drives labelled **identification**,** introjection** and **external regulation**.\\n\\n#### Identification\\nIdentification Is the strongest of the three extrinsic motivators. This is when you realize that **your contribution is important**, whether it be that you are a valued member of a sports team, or you realize that your participation and presence in classes or training is important for you to reach your own personal goal. It is the **closest to intrinsic motivation**, because you have solid logic and are interested in improving, but some of the enjoyment is missing. \\n\\n#### Introjection\\nWhen you are feeling **pressured** to do something, and the **guilt and anxiety** you get from either not doing something, or not doing it well, is driving you, that is introjection. Many people feel pressured to be ‘in shape’, or change their habits to fit in or work towards a goal that someone else has potentially set for you. This is a more **negative drive** that can easily be discouraging.\\n\\n#### External regulation \\nMotivation from **material rewards and praise or punishment** is fairly common, and how most people try to start up habits.. Doing things to get a treat or avoid criticism isn’t always bad, but it is one of the weakest motivations. Punishing yourself for doing something wrong or failing to reach your goals and thus, not getting your praise or reward can easily **break down your will to keep going**. \\n\\nNot seeing the right numbers on the scale, or having a bad workout can cause you to slip down into **amotivation**, where you see no reason to continue working towards that goal. You feel like you have no control, and doing that workout can’t possibly get you from point A to point B, so why do it at all?  \\n\\n\\n![Accomplishment](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/fitness/23-the-science-of-motivation/motivation-accomplishment.jpg \\\"Man accomplished his goal\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Roadblocks\\nEveryone runs into problems. Different people, depending on their gender, age, environment, ext, experience different issues. In the beginning there can be **self consciousness, the fear of failing, lack of social support, health problems, lack of strength, facilities, time and energy**… There is also **plateaus** and times where you **fall out of habits** that once were once really strong. \\n\\nIn order to keep climbing and improving, you have to get back up when life pushes you down. Solving your problems can be rewarding in itself, so it’s worth it to **fight your way over those blocks**, and take a big step towards that stronger motivation when you finally get past it. \\n\\n\\n### Jumping Hurdles\\nThe first step in getting past barriers is figuring out what they are, and the second step is tackling them **one by one, step by step**. Some ways to work past the above problems are: \\n\\n- Set **personal goals** for yourself, and don’t do things for the sake of others opinions of you (focus on yourself, not others). Continue to meet those small goals to give yourself **positive reinforcement to continue**.\\n\\n- Make your goals **S.M.A.R.T. Specific, measurable, attainable, realistic, and timely**. If your goals are very reasonable and you can achieve them easily, you will be more likely to set your goals higher as you continue, and **believe in yourself and your ability to achieve them**. \\n\\n- Learn the **benefits for health**, to improve your **abilities and quality of life**, don’t just focus on your weight or appearance. \\n\\n- Find **care and support** from mentors like parents, co-workers, trainers, coaches and peers. It can be a strong drive, especially when their feedback is clear, rational, and gives you more information to self-drive and self-support as you solve problems on your own. \\n\\n- **Plan and organize** yourself to allow proper time to work on and achieve your goals. \\n\\n- **Positivity is key to success**, and success grows exponentially when it is reinforced, so it’s important that you set and reach each of those goals so you can **see and feel your growth and improvement**.  \\n\\n- **Stress free environments** like your home can reduce pressure so you can learn at your pace. The same goes for finding a gym with an atmosphere that suits you (smaller and calmer vs larger and louder, or geared towards your activity).\\n\\n\\n### Conclusion\\nHaving extrinsic motivation for something does not mean you will not succeed. Everyone starts somewhere, and strong intrinsic motivation doesn’t appear overnight. Be **persistent, consistent and positive, build interest and challenge yourself** in order to strengthen your **self-drive to succeed**. \\n\\n**Satisfaction** comes with **believing** that you can do something, **achieving** those goals and **improving** yourself. Always remind yourself why you do what you do, and you will succeed. \\n\\n\\n**I want to. It makes me feel good.**\\n<br>\\n**I am worth this, and so it is worth my time.**  \\n\\n<iframe width=\\\"560\\\" height=\\\"315\\\" src=\\\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Wwkgsy-9GeA\\\" frameborder=\\\"0\\\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\\n\\n\\n<p class=\\\"references\\\">\\n<strong>References</strong>: <br>\\nRichard, M., et al. \\\"Intrinsic motivation and exercise adherence.\\\" Int J Sport Psychol 28.4 (1997): 335-354.\\n<br>\\nPelletier, Luc G., et al. \\\"Toward a new measure of intrinsic motivation, extrinsic motivation, and amotivation in sports: The Sport Motivation Scale (SMS).\\\" Journal of sport and Exercise Psychology 17 (1995): 35-35.\\n<br>\\nKarvitz, L. \\\"Exercise Motivation: What Starts and Keeps People Exercising.\\\"University of New Mexico (2011).\\n</p>\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-10-17T15:05:25.680Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-11-09T04:10:59.042Z\",\"userId\":56,\"categories\":[{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Category\",\"data\":{\"id\":2,\"className\":\"Category\",\"title\":\"Articles: Fitness\",\"description\":\"Fitness model interviews, workout advice and everything related to the fitness lifestyle. Frozen\\n## Make Use Of Your Frozen Fruits And Vegetables\\n\\n\\nThere are tons of recipes using fresh fruits and vegetables, but the fear of **fresh foods going bad** and the cost of **constantly buying more fresh produce** can be daunting. \\n\\nGymaholic busts the myth about freezing killing nutrition, and shows you some recipes to get creative with any frozen fruits and vegetables you might have hidden in your freezer.\\n\\n\\n![Vegetables](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/27-fresh-vs-frozen-fruits-vegetables/vegetables.jpg \\\"Looks delicious\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Myth: Frozen Produce Has Lower Nutritional Value. \\nSome people are convinced that because produce has been frozen the nutritional value can be cut down. If you are one of these people, rest assured that this myth has been totally busted. **There is no significant loss in nutritional value from freezing!**\\n\\nOf course, with improper storing or packaging you can freezer burn anything, but if you just keep things sealed well, there’s very little value lost over several months. **Stock up your freezers, because they aren’t just used for meat!** \\n\\n\\n\\n### Food and Heat\\nIf you don’t lose nutritional value from freezing, are there any ways you can lose nutritional value? It’s actually **during the cooking process**. **Heat can denature proteins and destroy vitamins and minerals** in foods, so **overcooking** vegetables is where you can lose some nutrition.  \\n\\nThe **most nutritious to least nutritious** ways to cook vegetables are:\\n- Raw\\n- Steamed\\n- Boiled\\n- Baked\\n- Fried\\n\\nEven so, all of these cooking methods shouldn’t take away enough vitamins and antioxidants for you to worry. \\n\\nWhat takes away the ‘healthiness’ from the dish you’re making is more likely the oil, butter and salt used to stop it from sticking, add flavor and keep moisture in your cooking. **Baking and frying tempt you to add more fats, whereas water-based cooking reduces that need**.\\n\\n\\n### Cost and Health Benefits.\\nMore is better! ...When it comes to fruits and vegetables, that is. A ton of people specifically **don’t get enough vegetables**, and some people don’t eat a ton of fruit either! They contain powerful **antioxidants, vitamins and minerals galore, and healthy fibre**. \\n\\nFrozen packages of fruit and vegetables aren’t always cheaper than fresh produce, but they do have the **value of convenience**. They also **often contain larger amounts, and higher quality** produce than the fresh produce you may have to pick through and choose yourself. \\n\\nYou also save time by buying canned or frozen, because they are **often already cut up and ready to use**. There is no clock ticking down the time you have to use them, which saves waste, and thus can also save you even more money.\\n\\n\\n![Fruits](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/27-fresh-vs-frozen-fruits-vegetables/fruits.jpg \\\"Looks good\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Conclusion\\nFind any ways you can **add more fruits and vegetables to your diet**, the more, the better! **Whether it be fresh, canned or frozen**, don’t be afraid to add more vegetables to your meals. Your body will thank you.\\n\\nWith all that being said, here are some **highly customizable recipes** for breakfast, lunch and dinner, so you can get some use out of that frozen produce. The recipe ingredients and directions are down below! \\n\\n<iframe width=\\\"560\\\" height=\\\"315\\\" src=\\\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/EXOUNb-_ZZE\\\" frameborder=\\\"0\\\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\\n\\n<p class=\\\"references\\\">\\n<strong>References</strong>: <br>\\nMiglio, Cristiana, et al. \\\"Effects of different cooking methods on nutritional and physicochemical characteristics of selected vegetables.\\\" Journal of agricultural and food chemistry 56.1 (2007): 139-147.\\n<br>\\nFavell, D. J. \\\"A comparison of the vitamin C content of fresh and frozen vegetables.\\\" Food chemistry 62.1 (1998): 59-64.\\n<br>\\nDanesi, F., and A. Bordoni. \\\"Effect of home freezing and Italian style of cooking on antioxidant activity of edible vegetables.\\\" Journal of food science73.6 (2008): H109-H112.\\n</p>\\n\\n\\n### Recipes\\n\\n#### Breakfast ‘Icecream’\\nYep, you read that right. Icecream for breakfast? It’s like frozen yogurt in the morning without all the added sugar, and you still get the fun of adding your favourite crunchy toppings! For this recipe you will need:\\n\\n- 1-2 Cups of Frozen Fruit\\n- ½-1 Cup of Milk (Dairy or Non-Dairy) \\n- ½ Cup Greek Yogurt (0% Vanilla Recommended) \\n\\nPut all three into a small blender and blend until smooth (You can also double the amounts in a large blender and freeze half!). If the blend is too liquidy, add more frozen fruit and yogurt to make it as thick as you want. If your mix gets too thick and blocks some of the frozen pieces from getting blended, add more milk. \\n\\nYou can also add a scoop of your favourite protein powder, flax or chia seeds, and even a chunk of frozen spinach directly into the main icecream blend! Some topping ideas for your icecream are:\\n\\n- Your Favourite Granola\\n- Sunflower, Pumpkin, Flax and Chia... Seeds\\n- Pecans, Almonds, Cashew... Nuts\\n- Shredded or Flakes of Coconut \\n- Fresh Fruit or Warmed Frozen Fruit\\n\\n\\n#### Pasta Salad\\nPasta salad is a classic, and there are so many variations it’s hard to go wrong. There are tons of different types of pasta to choose from, but here’s my general guidelines, and my recipe for the dressing:\\n\\n- 2-3 Cups Pasta (Reg, Whole Wheat or a Mix of Both)\\n- 1-2 Cup Fresh Vegetables (Peppers, Cucumber, Onion, Tomato...) \\n- 1 Cup Frozen or Canned Vegetables (Edamame, Corn, Green Peas, Chickpeas, Beans…)\\n- 1 Cup Cheese Cubes (Optional) \\n¼-½ Cup Dressing*\\n\\n**Dressing**\\n\\nSometimes I like to have store bought dressing, but I extend it and cut down on the sugar added to them by only using a small amount and combining it with my homemade dressing. ****Optional**** Replace 1-2 Tbsp Oil with Italian Dressing \\n\\n- 2-4 Tbsp Extra Virgin Olive Oil\\n- 1 Tbsp Apple Cider Vinegar\\n- 1 Tbsp Paprika\\n- 1 Tbsp Oregano\\n- 1 Tbsp Onion Salt\\n- 1 Tbsp Garlic Powder\\n- Salt & Pepper\\n\\nCook the pasta, and then mix the frozen vegetables in with it to thaw them and cool the pasta down. Chop all fresh vegetables into small pieces, the cheese into small cubes and drain and rinse any canned beans/peas. \\n\\nOnce the pasta is cool enough that it won’t melt the cheese, you can mix everything together, add half the dressing and stick it in the fridge. Pasta salad is much better when it’s cold, and the salad will soak up some of the dressing in the fridge, so add a bit more dressing after a couple hours in the fridge, mix it up and you’re good to go!\\n\\n\\n#### Fried Rice\\nThink it’s hard to make healthier fried rice? Think again! Fried rice is super easy, and very versatile with what vegetables you can add to it. The one thing to remember is that you’ll get the best tasting fried rice if you **cook the rice the day before**, and just heat it up in the pan. \\n\\nYou can also add some extra protein to your dish by mixing in cooked chicken, steak or salmon with the rice, or just serve cooked on top of the rice. ****Optional****  **Add Chicken Breast, Salmon Fillet, or Small Steak**.\\n\\n- 2-3 Tbsp Extra Virgin Olive Oil\\n- 1-2 Cups Fresh Vegetables (Carrots, Onions, - Broccoli, Peppers…)\\n- 1 Cup Frozen Vegetables (Edamame, Peas, - Carrots, Mixed Veg…)\\n- 2-3 Cups Cooked Rice (White, Brown, Mixed…) \\n- 2 Tbsp Soya Sauce \\n- 1-2 Tbsp Sesame Oil\\n- 1 Tbsp Garlic\\n- 1 Egg\\n\\nHeat a large skillet or wok on medium heat and add a bit of oil to the pan, leaving some on the side. Put all the vegetables in the pan and cook for a few minutes, tossing them in the oil.\\n\\nAdd in a tbsp of soya sauce and sesame oil, then toss and cook for another 5 minutes or until some of the vegetables get lightly browned. Add the rice, garlic, a little more extra virgin olive oil, soya sauce and sesame oil and toss together. Keep heating for another few minutes to warm and combine. \\n\\nMake an open space in the middle of the pan, scramble the egg in a dish and then put the egg in the open space. Let it cook for several seconds and then mix everything together and let it finish cooking in the rice and vegetables. Cook for another couple minutes until you’re satisfied everything is hot and cooked and serve! \",\"commentCount\":1,\"createdAt\":\"2016-06-15T02:45:13.891Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2017-04-20T11:18:15.818Z\",\"userId\":56,\"categories\":[{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Category\",\"data\":{\"id\":5,\"className\":\"Category\",\"title\":\"Articles: Nutrition\",\"description\":\"Nutrition advice food information and simple recipes to become healthy. There is a lot of information available in recent years that show plant-based diets can **improve our health** and the health of our planet too!\\n\\nIf you are starting to think about plant based diets like **pescetarianism, vegetarianism, veganism**, or anything in between, there are a few things you should think about first. Gymaholic give you some tips to get you started and push you in the right direction, showing you how to make a plant-based diets a long and happy lifestyle choice. \\n\\n\\n![Vegan tortillas](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/26-how-to-go-vegan-vegetarian/vegan-tortillas.jpg \\\"Looks delicious\\\")\\n\\n\\n### What it Means to Go Plant-Based\\nThe title ‘plant-based’ is fairly self explanatory, which is why it’s the focus of this article rather than vegetarian or vegan. There are different ‘levels’ of plant based diets, but they are just words that generally state what you eat without you having to explain it in more detail.\\n\\n**Pescetarians** generally do not eat meats, but they do eat **fish, eggs and dairy products**, and **do not try to avoid animal ‘ingredients’** like byproducts that come from various animals used as stabilizers (gelatin, ext.) and added ingredients in foods and cosmetics. \\n\\n**Vegetarian** is a wider term that can sometimes be similar to pescetarians. Vegetarians do not usually eat meat but there are some ‘part time’ or ‘flexible’ vegetarians that consume certain meats less frequently. They **may or may not eat fish, eggs or dairy products (Lacto-ovo vegetarian** is used for those who consume eggs and dairy). Often vegetarians also **do not try to avoid animal ‘ingredients’**. \\n\\n**Vegan** is essentially avoiding everything possible that does or could have come from an animal. It varies between people, but usually this includes **avoiding all meats, fish (and seafood), eggs, dairy (from any dairy producing animal) and any ingredients (gelatin, hormones, stabilizers, ext.) that are made from animal byproducts**. Some vegans include honey and bee-products, and extend their choices from food into items that include **leather and feathers**.  \\n\\n\\n### Why Go Plant-Based? \\nThere is a ton of evidence that people have written entire books on, showing the logical, physical and economical value of eating plant based diets-- But what it all comes down to is **you and your personal choice**. \\n\\nMany people want to be **healthier**, but more often there are a lot of **morals and beliefs** that come into play when dealing with animals, which push people to seek plant-based options. \\n\\nAlthough it is great to increase your intake of plant products over animal products simply because it can be healthier, you should do some research on the benefits of that choice, and think truly about **why you want to change**. Putting reasoning behind a decision can be a strong motivator, keeping you going and putting you back on track if you start to stray from your goals.\\n\\n\\n\\n### Is There Anyone That Shouldn’t? \\nYes and no. In the technical sense, anyone can live on a plant-based diet, even an extreme vegan diet. **Deciding whether a health condition would be worsened by a plant-based diet should be decided by your doctor and possibly a dietician**. \\n\\nThe problem with many people is that they **do not have the time and patience to learn** how to get what they need from plant sources and **make it enjoyable**. Others tend to tie **weight loss** to plant based diets, **which is not always an achieved benefit**. This is what causes most people to try and fail when suddenly switching to vegetarian/vegan. \\n\\nAll bodies and situations are different, so the way you tackle a plant-based diet needs to be **personalized to you and your daily life, body and activity level**, just like a non-vegetarian/vegan diet. If you want more information specifically on exercising and plant based diets, check out **<a href=\\\"/articles/nutrition/build-muscle-vegetarian-vegan-diet\\\" title=\\\"All you need to know about building muscle on a vegan diet\\\" data-navigation=\\\"external link - \\\" target=\\\"_blank\\\">building muscle on a vegetarian or vegan diet</a>**.\\n\\nSomeone who is heavily active needs to consume a lot more than someone who isn’t, and if you want to lose weight, you need to consume healthier sources of carbohydrates, fats and protein. Despite there being a lot of healthier options, there are **plant-based versions of most processed and junk foods too**. \\n\\nBelieve it or not, eating healthy for a vegetarian/vegan has similar problems to eating healthy as a non vegetarian/vegan. \\n\\n\\n![Vegan pastas](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/26-how-to-go-vegan-vegetarian/vegan-pasta.jpg \\\"Looks good\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Plant-Based (Vegetarian/Vegan)\\n\\n-   Processed and pre-made foods that are cheaper may taste bland.\\n\\n-   Processed and pre-made foods are expensive and taste better, but are likely high in simple sugars, fats, sodium... and bad for your health. \\n\\n-   Making your own food requires more learning and research into recipes and time to cook and prepare in advance. Trading in your time makes the price more manageable.\\n\\n\\n### Plant and Animal Based (Non-Vegetarian/Vegan) \\n\\n-   Processed and pre-made foods are cheaper and taste better, but are likely high in simple sugars, fats, sodium... and bad for your health. \\n\\n-   Processed and pre-made foods that are expensive may taste bland.\\n\\n-   Making your own food requires more learning and research into recipes and time to cook and prepare in advance. Trading in your time makes the price more manageable.\\n\\n\\nYou can see that the food industry has made it difficult for everyone to eat healthy. The best option is to **find the time to learn, prepare and cook things for yourself** so you can control the ingredients and make great tasting, healthy food for cheaper. With that said, let’s look at some tips to help you along the way! \\n\\n\\n### Let’s Get Started!\\n\\n-   **Go at your own pace.** Crash diets don’t work for a reason. The quicker and more dramatic your change is, the less likely it’s going to stick with you  for the long term.\\n\\n-   **Small changes and goals.** You do not have to throw out all the meat, eggs and/or dairy in your house and become vegan tomorrow. Slowly stop eating/buying one type of meat/animal product at a time over a period of a few weeks. \\n\\n-   **Don’t sweat the rules.** If you feel guilty every time you accidentally eat something that contains meat, you’re not going to have fun transitioning. It happens, and there are a lot of times when you’re first starting out that will feel like you don’t have a choice but to break the rules. Over time you can find ways to work around different situations to suit you. \\n\\n-   **Learn constantly.** The internet is your best friend. Look up ways to make plant-based versions of your favourite foods. Find cookbooks and websites with recipes and look up how to properly cook vegetarian/vegan ingredients.\\n\\n-  **Try new things.** A lot of great foods can come from different cultures, and when you need to eat plant-based, having variety can keep things new and fun. Branch out and eat vegetables you haven’t before, or try a new restaurant that has more vegetarian or vegan options. \\n\\n-   **Be prepared.** Preparing your own meals/snacks can help tremendously with cravings and if you are in a social situation, can reduce the stress put on others by what you want to eat. \\n\\n-   **Start at home.** When you go out to restaurants or social events sometimes there aren’t as many options for you. It’s okay to start with what you can control within your own home. Sometimes it can feel better to build new positive habits on your own without fear of judgement from others. \\n\\n-   **Respect others.** Others may not agree with your lifestyle, and you may not agree with theirs. It is not your place to judge their choices and not their place to judge yours. \\n\\n-    **Find support where you can.** There are tons of support groups online that can share stories and recipes. Find a friend that wants to try new things with you, or even just offer their moral support. \\n\\n\\n### Conclusion\\nIf this is something you want to do, stick with it, and take the time to work through problems instead of just giving up. **Make what you want and what you believe in a part of your life, and don’t let anything stop you.**\\n\\n\\nDo your best, remind yourself constantly why you want to do this and try to enjoy yourself as much as possible. **Work hard and stay strong!**\\n\\n\\n<iframe width=\\\"560\\\" height=\\\"315\\\" src=\\\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Z4kRvJ1blnQ\\\" frameborder=\\\"0\\\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-06-15T02:45:13.891Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-08-09T13:09:37.038Z\",\"userId\":56,\"categories\":[{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Category\",\"data\":{\"id\":5,\"className\":\"Category\",\"title\":\"Articles: Nutrition\",\"description\":\"Nutrition advice food information and simple recipes to become healthy. 8Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.118Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"articleId\":69,\"tagId\":2061}},\"cid\":29759},{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Tag\",\"data\":{\"id\":315,\"className\":\"Tag\",\"name\":\"fish\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:24:47.356Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:24:47.356Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"articleId\":69,\"tagId\":315}},\"cid\":29760},{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Tag\",\"data\":{\"id\":2063,\"className\":\"Tag\",\"name\":\"meat\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.130Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.130Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"articleId\":69,\"tagId\":2063}},\"cid\":29761},{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Tag\",\"data\":{\"id\":674,\"className\":\"Tag\",\"name\":\"foods\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:25:03.891Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-01-28T04:25:03.891Z\",\"ArticleTag\":{\"createdAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2016-08-03T03:41:34.150Z\",\"articleId\":69,\"tagId\":674}},\"cid\":29762}],\"user\":{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"User\",\"data\":{\"id\":56,\"className\":\"User\",\"createdAt\":\"2016-06-29T03:32:29.913Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2017-04-20T12:16:00.903Z\",\"email\":\"sara.pindera@gmail.com\",\"lastName\":\"Pindera\",\"firstName\":\"Sara\",\"name\":\"msmaddhatt\",\"role\":2,\"verifiedAt\":\"2017-04-20T12:16:00.903Z\",\"avatar\":\"https://static.tumblr.com/nc9sq5s/zQnojkn54/avatar_a42c77d7f844_128.png\",\"bio\":\"Bachelor of Science in Nutrition and Nutraceuticals. A Canadian with a love of food, fitness and health. \",\"website\":\"https://www.youtube.com/c/msmaddhatt/\",\"gender\":2,\"birthday\":\"1994-07-25T00:00:00.000Z\",\"height\":5.5,\"heightUnit\":1,\"weight\":120,\"weightUnit\":1,\"goal\":3,\"location\":\"CA\",\"timezone\":\"America/Toronto\"},\"cid\":2028}},\"cid\":1384},\"if-it-fits-your-macros\":{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Article\",\"data\":{\"id\":68,\"className\":\"Article\",\"title\":\"If It Fits Your Macros (IIFYM): Diet And Lifestyle\",\"description\":\"Gymaholic introduces you to IIFYM, shows you how to easily calculate your current macronutrients on your own, and change them to suit your goals. \",\"img\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/25-if-it-fits-your-macros/1-if-it-fits-your-macros.jpg\",\"shareImg\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/25-if-it-fits-your-macros/share-if-it-fits-your-macros-2.jpg\",\"slug\":\"if-it-fits-your-macros\",\"publishedAt\":\"2016-06-29T03:19:45.329Z\",\"content\":\"# If It Fits Your Macros (IIFYM) \\n## How to calculate your macronutrients\\n\\n\\nThere is a lot of information on the internet about macronutrients and the **“If It Fits Your Macros” (IIFYM) diet/lifestyle**. You can enter information about your sex, weight, height, ext, into an online macronutrient calculator and it will spit out a number of calories or some macronutrient ratios to follow. \\n\\nCalculating and following an IIFYM lifestyle may seem like a lot of work, but it doesn’t have to be! Gymaholic introduces you to IIFYM, shows you how to easily **calculate your current macronutrients** on your own, and **change them to suit your goals**. \\n\\n\\n![Nice burger](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/25-if-it-fits-your-macros/burger.jpg \\\"Looks delicious\\\")\\n\\n\\n### IIFYM Diet/Lifestyle\\nThe basis of IIFYM is that it doesn’t matter what it is you’re eating, as long as you reach your goal calories and macronutrients for the day. This gives you a type of freedom to eat whatever you want, which can be beneficial to people just starting to get interested in their health and people with advanced knowledge and skills. \\n\\nThe thing that separates a “diet” from a “lifestyle” is long-term stability. Technically you can eat whatever you want, but if all of your calories and macros are coming from fast-food, eventually there will be consequences. \\n\\nThis can be a great starting point for those trying to develop healthier habits, as you can stick with the same amount of calories and macros through the day, but start **experimenting by adding in healthier recipes, more fruits and vegetables, fibre and healthy fats**. \\n\\nIIFYM does require some tracking and monitoring, so if it adds too much stress or work to count your macros you may want to try another even simpler method like **<a href=\\\"/articles/nutrition/the-80-20-rule\\\" title=\\\"More info about the 80/20 diet\\\" target=\\\"_blank\\\">The 80/20 Rule</a>**. \\n\\nKeep in mind that **IIFYM** can also lead to some good habits like paying attention and **noticing what and how much you’re eating throughout the day**. Even if you don’t follow IIFYM, it could be helpful to calculate your calories and macros every once in awhile while working towards a goal. \\n\\n\\n### Calculating Calories and Macros\\nTo decide what your goal calories and macronutrients should be, you first have to find out how much of each you’re eating right now. It’s easiest to find an average, so record roughly how many **carbs, protein and fat you eat every day** to get an average amount of each. The calculations are really simple, but you’ll still probably have use a calculator to crunch the numbers. \\n\\nCalories are a measurement of **heat released or energy that can be used through the breakdown of the macronutrients**: carbohydrates, protein and fat. You don’t have to record calories, because you can calculate them through the macronutrients you record. \\n\\n**Carbohydrates and Protein → 4 calories per gram**\\n\\n**Fats → 9 calories per gram**\\n\\nTo calculate how many calories you’re getting from carbohydrates or protein, simply multiply the gram amount by 4. To calculate how many calories you’re getting from fat, simply multiply the gram amount by 9. For example, If you eat **150g of carbohydrates, 112g of protein and 50g of fat** in a day, your macronutrient calculations would look like this: \\n\\n150g carbs x 4 calories/g = 600 calories\\n\\n112g protein x 4 calories/g = 450 calories\\n\\n50g fat x 9 calories/g = 450 calories\\n\\nTotal Calories = 600 + 450 + 450 = 1500\\n\\n\\n### Macronutrient Ratios \\nMacronutrient ratios show you the **percentage of calories from each of the macronutrients out of your daily 100% calorie total**. The example above has a 40/30/30 ratio. \\n\\n600 calories / 1500 calorie total = 0.4 = **40% calories from carbohydrates**\\n\\n450 calories / 1500 calorie total = 0.3 = **30% calories from protein**\\n\\n450 calories / 1500 calorie total = 0.3 = **30% calories from fats**\\n\\nThis information can be used in multiple ways. **For example, If you want to increase your total calories to 1800, but keep your ratio the same** you can do all of these calculations backwards to find out how many calories would be coming from each of your macronutrients.  \\n\\n1800 x 0.4 = **720 calories from carbohydrates**\\n\\n1800 x 0.3 = **540 calories from protein and fat**\\n\\n720 calories / 4 cal/g = **180g carbohydrates**\\n\\n540 calories / 4 cal/g = **135g protein**\\n\\n540 calories / 9 cal/g = **60g fat**\\n\\nIf you wanted to keep the **calories the same (1500), but change the ratio to 50/30/20** you get different gram amounts of each macronutrients with the same calorie total.\\n\\n1500 x 0.5 = **750 calories from carbohydrates** (750/4 = 187g carbohydrates)\\n\\n1500 x 0.3 = **450 calories from protein** (450/4 = 112g protein)\\n\\n1500 x 0.2 = **300 calories from fat** (300/9 = 33g fat)\\n\\n\\n![Tortillas](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/25-if-it-fits-your-macros/tortillas.jpg \\\"Looks good\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Achieve Your Goals With IIFYM\\nJust like in the examples above, in order to lose weight, gain weight or maintain your current weight, you can **change your calories or change your macronutrient ratio**. The most important thing to remember is that everyone is different, so you will likely have to experiment to find the numbers that work for you, however, here are some good starting points. \\n\\nIf your goal is to **lose weight**, you can **decrease your total calories, or reduce the calories from carbohydrates**. You can reduce fat too, but fats (especially healthier fats) can be a lot less damaging to the body then excess glucose (simple sugars/carbohydrates) can be. \\n\\nWhen **reducing your calories** you want to start by reducing the total by **5-10%**. If you’re consuming 2000 calories, 2000 x 0.1 = 200 calories. After subtracting that 10% or 200 calories, your new total would be 1800 calories.\\n\\nIf you try that 1800 calories for a few weeks and find you aren’t progressing, or you keep that up for a few months and you hit a **fat loss plateau**, you can either reduce another 5-10% (1800x0.1 = 180, 1800-180= 1620 calories) or you can **change your macronutrient ratio**.\\n\\n**High Carb** - 60/25/15\\n\\n**Moderate Carb** - 50/30/20\\n\\n**Low-Moderate Carb** - 40/30/30\\n\\n**Low Carb** - 25/45/30\\n\\nIf you’re consuming 1800 calories and your ratio of **Carbohydrate/Protein/Fat** is 50/30/20, you could change that ratio to 40/35/25, 40/30/30 or 40/40/20… **It’s best to move slowly**, as it would be a bit dramatic to cut 50% carbs down to 30%, but as with before, if you try it for a few weeks or months and decide it’s not working or run into another plateau, you can change the ratio again until you find something that works.  \\n\\nWhen you’re looking to gain weight you can **increase your overall calories** by 5-10% or just like in weight loss, adjust your macronutrient ratio to **increase the calories coming from protein**. \\n\\n\\n### Conclusion\\nThere are so many ways to **progress towards and achieve your goals**. Calculating your macros and following and IIFYM \\nlifestyle could help you on it’s own, or be a **stepping stone to healthier habits**. Here are some things to remember: \\n\\n-   **You can eat whatever you want to fill your macros, but being mindful of what you’re eating can make IIFYM a lifestyle rather than a diet.**\\n\\n-   **Both carbohydrates and protein have 4 calories per gram, and fat has 9 calories per gram.**\\n\\n-   **Calculating your total calories and macronutrient ratios can help you see more clearly what you’re eating now.**\\n\\n-   **Changing the total calories by about 5-10% or adjusting your macronutrient ratio can help you towards your goals and push you past a plateau. **\\n\\n\\nAlways keep learning and growing. You can do this!\\n\\n\\n<iframe width=\\\"560\\\" height=\\\"315\\\" src=\\\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/7lfJBkPmtKQ\\\" frameborder=\\\"0\\\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\",\"commentCount\":1,\"createdAt\":\"2016-06-15T02:45:13.891Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2017-04-20T11:26:15.807Z\",\"userId\":56,\"categories\":[{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Category\",\"data\":{\"id\":5,\"className\":\"Category\",\"title\":\"Articles: Nutrition\",\"description\":\"Nutrition advice food information and simple recipes to become healthy. of Science in Nutrition and Nutraceuticals. A Canadian with a love of food, fitness and health. \",\"website\":\"https://www.youtube.com/c/msmaddhatt/\",\"gender\":2,\"birthday\":\"1994-07-25T00:00:00.000Z\",\"height\":5.5,\"heightUnit\":1,\"weight\":120,\"weightUnit\":1,\"goal\":3,\"location\":\"CA\",\"timezone\":\"America/Toronto\"},\"cid\":2029}},\"cid\":1385},\"carb-cycling-keto-diets\":{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Article\",\"data\":{\"id\":67,\"className\":\"Article\",\"title\":\"Carb Cycling: The Targeted and Cyclic Ketogenic Diets\",\"description\":\"Gymaholic will show you the different kinds of ketogenic diets, and help you decide if one of them might be a good tool to help you reach your goals. \",\"img\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/24-carb-cycling-keto-diets/1-carb-cycling-keto-diets.jpg\",\"shareImg\":\"//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/24-carb-cycling-keto-diets/share-carb-cycling-keto-diets-1.jpg\",\"slug\":\"carb-cycling-keto-diets\",\"featuredAt\":\"2016-06-18T06:02:53.267Z\",\"publishedAt\":\"2016-06-15T03:48:19.057Z\",\"content\":\"# Carb Cycling\\n## The Targeted and Cyclic Ketogenic Diets\\n\\nYou may have heard of **‘carb cycling’**, but hearing about a new kind of diet through the fitness community grapevine doesn’t always mean it’s right for you. Gymaholic will show you the **different kinds of ketogenic diets** and help you decide if one of them might be a good tool to help you reach your goals. \\n\\nThere is the **Standard Ketogenic Diet (SKD)**, and the modified versions of the SKD, which are the **Targeted Ketogenic Diet (TKD)** and the **Cyclic Ketogenic Diet (CKD)**, which is more commonly known as carb cycling. \\n\\n\\n![Nice burger](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/24-carb-cycling-keto-diets/burger-no-bun.jpg \\\"Looks delicious\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Standard Ketogenic Diet (SKD)\\n<a href=\\\"/articles/nutrition/58/weight-loss-ketogenic-and-low-carb-diets\\\" title=\\\"More info about keto diets\\\" target=\\\"_blank\\\">There has already been an article published on **ketogenic diets**</a>, but that article specifically covers the **standard ketogenic diet (SKD).** This diet is great for fat loss, and low levels of activity are known to increase the benefits of ketosis.\\n\\nWhen your body is deprived of <a href=\\\"/articles/nutrition/47/carbohydrates-fuel-your-body\\\" title=\\\"All you need to know about carbs\\\" target=\\\"_blank\\\">**carbohydrate (glucose) energy**</a>, it enters **ketosis**, which is when your body relies mainly on **fat for energy**. When fats are broken down by the liver, you get **ketone bodies**, hence the name “keto”sis.\\n\\nUnder normal circumstances, we operate in a state of **glycolysis**, when **glucose** is broken down and used for energy. Ketosis usually occurs when the body is in a **‘fasted’ state**, and low on carbohydrate fuel. It is the body state where you **burn the most fat**. You can trick your body into the fasted state by following a **‘low’ or ‘very low’ carbohydrate, moderate to high fat and moderate to high protein diet.**\\n\\nFor someone eating **2000 calories a day, a ‘low’ carbohydrate diet** is usually around **130g of carbs per day**, or about **26% of your calories from carbohydrates**. A **‘very low’ carbohydrate diet has significantly less, around 50g of carbohydrates per day**, or around **10% calories from carbohydrates**. The rest of your calories come from protein and fats.\\n\\n\\n#### Problems with SKD\\nIf you have medical problems you should consult your doctor first before trying any sort of ketogenic diet. There are also some possible side effects like **fatigue, dehydration and vitamin deficiencies** that can occur while your body adjusts to ketosis. \\n\\nAnother problem is that unfortunately, the standard ketogenic diet isn’t sustainable for individuals who are moderately to heavily active because the **carbohydrate intake is too low.**\\n\\nWeightlifters, bodybuilders and other sport athletes, **especially those who do short, powerful bursts of energy**, simply can’t function on a ketogenic diet. ‘Short term’ energy is provided by **carbohydrate (glucose and glycogen) stores in the body**, and since there is a limited amount that the body stores, when that runs out fat stores must be used.\\n\\nFat however, **cannot be metabolized for energy as fast as carbohydrates** (they are a ‘long term’ endurance energy source), so that high powered activity can’t be continued and that person will fatigue much faster. **There is also a higher chance of losing lean muscle mass**.\\n\\nSo what is the solution for those athletes that want to keep fat at bay, but maintain their lean muscle mass and energy while exercising? **The targeted ketogenic diet (TKD)** and the **cyclic ketogenic diet (CKD)**, also known commonly as ‘carb cycling’.\\n\\n\\n#### Summary (SKD)\\n- **<a href=\\\"/articles/nutrition/58/weight-loss-ketogenic-and-low-carb-diets\\\" title=\\\"More info about keto diets\\\" target=\\\"_blank\\\">Low carbohydrate diets promote ketosis and fat burning.</a>**\\n\\n- **Adjusting to ketosis can cause fatigue, dehydration and vitamin deficiencies.**\\n\\n- **SKD can only support minimal to beginner exercise levels and could potentially cause loss of muscle mass if more active.**\\n\\n\\n\\n### Targeted Ketogenic Diet (TKD)\\nIn the **targeted ketogenic diet**, carbohydrates are consumed immediately around exercise to refill those glycogen stores for **sustaining exercise and preventing lean muscle mass loss**, without affecting the fat burning effects of ketosis. However, this diet **will not increase your muscle mass or strength**.\\n\\nThis is a stepping stone between the SKD and CKD. You are leaving ketosis for a short period of time, but not for over a day (like in carb cycling). This diet can handle fairly intense exercise, so it can be used for **people who exercise frequently at beginner and intermediate levels**. \\n\\nA little experimentation is required to decide how much carbohydrates you should consume and how long before a workout you should consume them. Everyone is different, but somewhere between **25-50g of carbohydrates, <a href=\\\"/articles/nutrition/50/what-you-should-eat-before-after-workout\\\" title=\\\"What to eat before and after a workout\\\" target=\\\"_blank\\\">around 30 mins before your workout</a> is a good place to start**. Post workout carbs should not be taken unless you feel you need them because you want the body to return to ketosis as quickly as possible. \\n\\nSimple, sugary carbs are usually the carbohydrates of choice because the **glucose (sugar)** is digested and released quickly into the blood. The spike of the hormone insulin that follows causes that glucose to be taken up and stored in the muscle.\\n\\n\\n#### Problems with TKD\\n\\nTKD has similar problems as SKD. It is still a ketogenic diet so you would likely experience the same side effects of your body adjusting to it. With the TKD **it may take longer for your body to adjust to ketosis** since you are going in and out of it. \\n\\nPromoting consumption of **sugary carbs can hurt those trying to develop a healthy relationship with food**. Alongside that, if you attempt TKD with very **minimal exercising as an excuse to consume higher carbs**, you may not see the results you want. \\n\\n\\n#### Summary (TKD)\\n\\n- **Low carbohydrate diets promote ketosis and fat burning. It will not increase muscle mass or strength**.\\n\\n- **Consuming extra carbs around your workout keeps fatigue at bay and reserves muscle mass**.\\n\\n- **Can support beginner to intermediate activity/exercise levels**.\\n\\n- **Adjusting to ketosis can cause fatigue, dehydration and vitamin deficiencies. Constantly readjusting can prolong these effects.**\\n\\n\\n![Omelette](//cdn.gymaholic.co/articles/nutrition/24-carb-cycling-keto-diets/ketogenic-meal.jpg \\\"Looks amazing\\\")\\n\\n\\n### Cyclic Ketogenic Diet (CKD)\\n\\nThe cyclic ketogenic diet, also known as “**carb cycling**” is the most extreme modification of the SKD. Instead of just consuming carbohydrates before or around your exercise times you **cycle through “high carb” (around 2-3g/lb in males), “low carb” (around 0.5-1.5g/lb in males) and “no carb” days** fairly equally through the week. \\n\\n“No carb” days are technically just very low carbohydrate days, because **it is nearly impossible to achieve no carbs**. This is why vegetables are consumed on all days, and **should not count towards your carbohydrate total. A lot of water should also be consumed**.\\n\\nThe purpose of this diet is the same as the TKD: **refill muscle glucose/glycogen to sustain performance and prevent the loss of lean muscle mass**. However, the carbohydrates are increased more, for even longer for those at a **frequent, advanced exercise level**. \\n\\n**High carb days** are for the most **heavy and challenging workout days**, and then you rotate through low and ‘no’ carb days following. If you work out in the morning, it’s recommended to have a **low carb day before a high carb day** and/or ensure you consume enough carbs before your workout in order to get the benefits. \\n\\n**Consuming carbs after your workout** can be a bit more helpful in the CKD because you want to refill the glycogen stores to prepare for the next workout, which can take over 24 hours. The order of the carb cycle can be changed to **jump start fat loss** if you reach a plateau, or **increase your energy** if you feel that your glycogen stores may be lacking before a workout in a current schedule.\\n\\n\\n#### 7 Day Examples: \\nLow | High | No | High | Low | High | No… For scattered heavy workouts.\\n\\nNo | Low | No | Low | High | Low | High… For a heavier weekend recovery.\\n\\n\\n#### Problems with CKD\\n\\nThe same problems can occur as with both the SKD and TKD, with the **side effects of adjusting to ketosis**. The extremes of going between carb heavy and ketosis could potentially make these side effects worse or better, it depends on the individual and the cycle they choose to follow. This diet should most certainly not be undertaken by anyone who had medical problems without speaking to a doctor first. \\n\\nThis is a bad diet choice for anyone who is not **frequently and intensely active**. If there is no exercise to drain the glycogen/glucose stores so they can be refilled, if there is not enough fat being burned, there is potential to **gain weight**. This diet can keep you lean, and protect that lean muscle mass from being catabolized, but it **will not increase muscle mass and strength gains**.\\n\\nThe constant changes between high carbs and very low carbs can encourage a **binging and purging mentality**, but can also cause other problems as well. There is little information on the problems caused by jumping into ketosis and then binging on carbs and spiking insulin, but **if you have medical problems it could potentially put you in danger**.\\n\\n\\n#### CKD Summary\\n\\n- **Low carbohydrate diets promote ketosis and fat burning. It will not increase muscle mass or strength**.\\n\\n- **Having full days of increased carbohydrates can better support intermediate and advanced activity levels, keeps fatigue at bay and preserves muscle mass**.\\n\\n- **For beginners to intermediates it could cause weight gain and may promote binging and purging**.\\n\\n- **Adjusting to a combination of ketosis and high carb consumption can cause undetermined side effects. If you have medical problems it could potentially put you in danger**. \\n\\n\\n### Conclusion\\nKetogenic diets are not for everyone, but there are a few variations on the standard ketogenic diet that may be a better fit to your lifestyle. They can be easier to execute because you are simply watching your macros, but things can get more complicated if you are more active.\\n\\n\\nWork hard and stay safe!\\n\\n\\n<p class=\\\"references\\\">\\n<strong>References</strong>: <br>\\nHartnett, Thomas. \\\"Carb Cycling: Is It All It's Cracked Up To Be?.\\\". \\n<br>\\nSeidell, J. C., et al. \\\"The Science Behind The “Low Carb Flu”, and How To Regain Your Metabolic Flexibility.\\\" Int J Obes Relat Metab Disord 16.9 (1992): 667-74.\\n<br>\\nMcDonald, Lyle. \\\"The ketogenic diet.\\\" Macdonald, Austin, TX (1998).\\n<br>\\nDate, Join. \\\"An In-Depth Look Into Carbing Up On The Cyclical Ketogenic Diet With Lyle Mcdonald.\\\"\\n</p>\\n\\n\",\"commentCount\":1,\"createdAt\":\"2016-06-15T02:45:13.891Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2017-04-20T12:00:17.409Z\",\"userId\":56,\"categories\":[{\"changed\":{},\"error\":null,\"validation\":null,\"status\":\"STATUS_SUCCESS\",\"className\":\"Category\",\"data\":{\"id\":5,\"className\":\"Category\",\"title\":\"Articles: Nutrition\",\"description\":\"Nutrition advice food information and simple recipes to become healthy.
